## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science / solid mechanics)
**Analysis**: The variables stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T) indicate a constitutive law for material deformation, where stress depends on mechanical strain and thermal state. This belongs to the domain of materials science / mechanics of materials, specifically the modeling of flow curves or stress–strain relationships at elevated temperatures, often using thermal softening, strain hardening, and thermal expansion effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermo-elastic: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress due to mechanical strain after thermal expansion subtraction)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear thermal softening/hardening of stiffness)
- Power-law strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type work hardening)
- Power-law hardening with linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T) (softening factor linear in temperature)
- Power-law hardening with exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (typical thermal softening factor for flow stress)
- Voce-type saturation hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturating strain hardening combined with linear thermal effect)
- Ludwik-type hardening with additive temperature effect: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * T (additive influence of temperature on flow stress)
- Exponential strain hardening and thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (rapid initial hardening followed by saturation, with thermal factor)
- Temperature-dependent yield plus power-law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (yield stress linear in T, plus strain hardening)
- Polynomial strain hardening with thermal multiplier: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(c3 * T) (second-order strain effect combined with exponential thermal dependence)
- Hyperbolic-tangent saturation with thermal scaling: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (smooth saturation of stress with strain under thermal activation)
- Inverse temperature scaling of flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (Arrhenius-like thermal activation combined with power-law strain hardening)
- Arrhenius-like thermal softening of yield stress: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 / T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature-activated yield plus strain hardening)
- Sigmoidal strain hardening with temperature factor: sigma = c0 / (1 + exp(-c1 * (epsilon - c2))) * (1 + c3 * T) (sigmoidal transition to high stress, scaled by temperature)
- Zener-Hollomon type: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (creep-like constitutive equation adapted to strain and temperature, capturing power-law breakdown)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening is typically multiplicative: a factor that decreases with rising temperature, often exp(-c*T) or (1 - c*(T - T_ref)**m)
- Plastic strain hardening often follows a power law sigma ~ epsilon**n, where n is the strain hardening exponent
- Yield stress (initial sigma at epsilon=0) often depends linearly on temperature: sigma_y = c0 + c1*T (or c0 - c1*T for softening)
- Flow stress at large strains may saturate, captured by terms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon)
- Strain and temperature effects frequently combine multiplicatively: sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), assuming separable influences
- Thermal expansion introduces an effective mechanical strain offset: mechanical strain = total strain - alpha*T, leading to sigma ~ epsilon - c*T
- Higher-order strain terms (e.g., epsilon**2) can capture gradual changes in work hardening rate
